@w\mb [9] {(29 May)}\!  Date in Adobe text, p 3, changed here. This gaol delivery record is dated 29 May 1276 (see Doc descript.).  The incident behind it is dated Tuesday before Annunciation, i.e., 24 March 1275/6, as in text note below.  30 January 1275/6 is a Thursday.

@r\@i\An order for a ffeaste@i@r\! 
Also we haue ordeyned that eu{er}y yere yn the feste of the natiuite of Seynt iohn the baptyst a solempne obbite to be holde while the worlde stondyth. furst for oure founder William | swayne and <.>ristin his wyf and all his childeren and for his fader soule and moder soule and for all his frendis soulis and for all the bretherne and susterne soulis of oure said craft that be oute of this world dissesed yn seynt thomas churche of salesbury in the chaple of sent iohn the baptist that is to say on the euen the dirige by note and yn the morow the masse of requiem by note which masse to be gyune whanne matens be done at x at the cloke and that oure said wardens stiwardis and chamberlaynes wyt all oure hole craft and fraternite and oure s{er}uantis to be attendynd vppon the maire of the cite for the tyme beyng and other worshipful wyt hym of the same to bryng ynne the light of oure said fraternite from the chaundelerishous vnto the said seynt thomas churche ynto seynt iohn ys chaple ther and there to abide at the masse and offre at the same all oure craft and whiche of our said craft lakke and be not at the said masse and offeryng there of he to lese to oure said craft j lb of wex wyth oute a lawfull excuse y made to the wardens and to the stiwardis and that the to stiwardys for the tyme beyng eu{er}y yere shall make and sette a fore seynt iohn the baptist vppon the auter ij tap{er}s of j lb of wex and a garlond of roses to be sette vppon seynt iohnys hed and that the chaple to be strawed wyt grene russhis and wh{a}nne masse is done we all to go to gyder to oure place accustomed where oure dyner shall be holden wyt yn the said cite and there to abyde at dyner and sett till we haue dyned for the which dyn{e}r eu{er}y maister of oure said craft shall pay for hym and his wyf xij d. and for here  soper, if they woll come ther to, for the same money; a man alone viii d. a woman a lone vj d. and no dyner nether fest lenger by vs to be kepte saue only the same day and yerly to be kepte while the world stondith and soche p{er}sones of oure craft as hath promysed oure stiwardis to come to dyner and comyth not they shall pay eu{er}ich of them viij d. to the vse of the stiwardis of the said fraternite which muste nedes do the cost of that day.! 
Also we haue ordeyned that at the sayd fest and dyner atte soche oure seruantis called iorne men as be wyt yn oure said craft shall serue the maystres of oure craft in the tyme of bryngyng ynne of oure light and at oure feste and dyner there abydyng wyt vs at dyner atte soche place as the maysters and wardens wyll assigne at which dyner euery s{er}uant to pay iiij d. and that oure sayd stiwardes whanne the maist{r}es ben serued yn at the furst cource they shall p{ur}wey an honest place for all soche s{er}uantis to be sette at a borde or bordes conuenyently wyt yn the same place and to be serued by the apprentices [<.>] the maisters assigneme{n}t conueniently for here degre and than for the  secunde cours of the maisters by the said stiwardis they to be warned to a ryse and for to s{er}ue ynlyke wyse the said maiste{r}s as they did the furst cours and then they to goo to theire playce ayen and to ber s{er}ued ayen of theyre seconde cours makyng theym as myry as they can.! 
...!

@w\f 150 {(Minutes)}\! 
! 
Atte this p{re}sent assemble the mayre and Co{mmo}nialte of this Cite hath graunted vnto the iij mynstrell{es} of this [fo] Cite for the tyme beynge everth of theym a te{neme}nte atte Rolleston frely w{i}t{h}out payment of any rente theroff yeldynge to theym excepte that everthe off theym shall stonde to the Charge of the rep{ar}ac{i}on of his owen hous suffi{c}iently to be done! 
!

@h\SAR!1530--1!STG2\!)}\!  Note, re date, REED’s confusing of Thomas, apostle (recte) with Thomas abp (Becket).  Date should be 3 July – translation of St Thomas the apostle.  See comment below. 
@w\f 18 col 2* {(9 January 1530/1—8 January 1531/2) (3 July 1531) }\[[ ## no regular asccount year [[??]]. dating problem here: this St Thomas 29 Dec HVIII 23 = 1531—2. St Osmunds eve next coming is in 1532 UPDATE: I had doubts but I’ve double checked and this does say ‘die s{an}c{t}i Thome ep{iscop}i [anno regni regis henrici viij xxiij’ so the date of this convocatio is 29 Dec 1531. FURTHER UPDATE: all other assemblies of this type held in early July and is in yearly sequence so this must be the translation of the bishop 7 July [No, apostle, 3 July].]]  [[Re above violet comments: 1. There is no saint Thomas ‘ep[iscopus]’; the two saint Thomases relevant here are a) St Thomas archiep[iscopus] et m[artyr] – i.e., Thomas Becket, archbishop of Canterbury, murdered in the cathedral; and b) St Thomas ap[ostle], an original disciple, of doubting Thomas fame.  This distinction would have been clearly understood by the guild at the time.  I think the above editorial comment may be based on a misreading of ‘ap’ (apostle) as ‘ep’ (bishop), a reading that could be checked again; if ‘ap’ is correct, the record should be dated 3 July 1531, in reference to the date of the translation of St Thomas the apostle. AD.]]
...!

@w\single mb* {(after 28 August)}\!

@m\To ye Kynge o{u}r souereyne lorde@m \! 
In hys moste hu{m}ble wyes shewithe & complaynythe to yo{u}r moste excellent hyghnes yo{u}r pore orat{o}r & hu{m}ble subiecte herry sutton that where as ye right honorable S{ir} Iohn Bowchyer knyght Erle of bathe beinge seased in hys demesne as of fe of & in ye late hovse or priory called ye blacke fryars w{i}t{h}in ye town of ffysherton nere vnto ye cite of newe saru{m} w{i}t{h}in yo{u}r graces The seid Iohn davye sayth y{a}t theseid byll of complaynt ys vncerteyn & Insuffycyent yn ye lawe to be aunsweryd vnto & ye matter theryn conteynyd craftelye ffayned & Imagined of malyes only to the entent to put the seid defend{ant} to vexatyon cost{es} Troble & expenc{es} & to none other Intent or purpose and albehyt that hyt wer trewe as yt ys not yette dyu{er}se & sondrye thyng{es} surmysed yn theseid byll be matters determynable at the com{m}on lawe lawe @f\ lawe lawe: {dittography} @f \ & not yn thye honorable cowrte whervnto he p{r}ayth to be remytted Neu{er}theles yff he shall be orderyd or compellyd by this honorable cowrte to make aunswer vnto theseid ffayned byll/ then ffor ffurther aunswer unto the same & ffor declaration of the trowth towchyng the p{re}myss{es} vnto thys honorable cowrte theseyd Iohn davye sayth that trewe yt ys that ye seyd ryght honorable Erle of Bathe was seasyd of & yn theseid howse of p{r}iorye latte callyd the blake ffryers as yn theseyd byll of complaynt yt ys allegyd/ and he beyng ther of seasyd at the ffeaste of seynt mich{a}ell yn xxxiij@s\ti@s \ yere of owre g{r}acys by oon George Snelgar hys bayly dyd demyse g{r}aunte & to fferme lett vnto theseid Iohn davye all the grownd{es} w{i}t{h}yn the p{re}cyncte & cyrcuyte of theseid late p{r}iorye or howse of ffryers those grownd{es} whervppon any howse or howses wer then beyng & sytuat & also those grownd{es} w{i}t{h}yn theseid p{re}cyncte or cyrcuyte vpponn\ the w{hi}ch any garden or gardens wer then made only exceptyd In suche maner y{a}t theseid Iohn davy sholde & of ryght haue by theseyd demyse vnto hym made all the voyde or vacant grow{n}d{es} w{i}t{h}yn theseyd p{re}cyncte or cyrcuyte To haue & to holde theseyd grownd{es} Except byfore exceptyd vnto ye seid Iohn & his assignes ffrom theseid ffeaste of seynt Mich{a}ell vntyll ye ffull ende & t{er}me of oon yere then nexte ensuynge ffully to be co{mp}letyd & endyd & so ffrom yere to yere at ye wyll & pleasure of theseyd Erle yeldyng & payng therfor yerely vnto theseyd Erle & to his heyers vj s. viij d. by vertu wherof theseid Iohn davy peaseably & lawfullye entred yn to all the fforeseyd grownd{es} Except byfore exceptyd & was & ys therof possessyd accordynge & ye Erbes & grasse of theseid grownd{es} excepte byfore exceptyd dyd then & yette dothe take co{n}sume & occupye to hys owne com{m}odyte & p{ro}fytte as lawfull hyt was & ys ffor hym to do/ and bycause y{a}t theseid Agnes late wyffe of theseid Iohn davye att dyu{er}se & sondry tymes dyd repayre & resorte vnto theseid grownd{es} ffor to take & vse ye p{re}myss{es} vnto theseid Iohn davye demysed or letten as ys aforeseyd as she of ryght owght to do Theseyd complayna{n}t to ye entent y{a}t he wolde putte the wyffe of ye seid Iohn Davy yn suche ffeare & drede y{a}t she sholde not any more resorte vnto theseid Grownd{es} but rather to p{ro}cure her seyd husbond to fforsake & yelde vppe hys estate & Interest yn or to thesame ffor the acco{m}plyssheme{n}t of his lewde & evyll purpose & mynde on a certeyn tyme when he p{er}ceyvyd the seyd Agnes to be w{i}t{h}yn the @a\seid@a \ cyrcuyte of theseid late p{r}iorye went vnto the howse w{i}t{h}yn theseid cyrcuyte whyche he then hadde by the lycens of theseid Erle ffor the p{re}s{er}uation & kepyng of theseid beers & dyd lose & vntye ye grettyste & moste terryble bere that he then ther hadde & turnyd theseid grette bere vntyed & at large toward{es} theseid agnes and when she p{er}ceyvyd theseid bere to be at lybertye & com{m}yng nere toward{es} her she was sore affrayed & abasshede & ffor ffere w{i}t{h} asmyche spede as she myght ran ffrom theseid grett bere & by her hastye run{n}yng beyng yn suche grette ffere of theseid bere toke a sore ffall ageynst a grett peace of ledde lying yn the grownd callyd a sow of ledde w{i}t{h} the w{hi}ch ffall then & ther taken & hadde theseid agnes late wyffe unto ye seid Iohn davy ageynste whom also theseid byll of complaynt ys seid complayna{n}t may be cordyngly ponysshed ffor his seyd malycyouse & myschevouse offence yn y{a}t behalffe com{m}ytted & don w{i}t{h}out y{a}t that theseid Iohn davy & agnes or any of them @w\f 42* {(10 January 1564—8 January 1565) (14 October 1564)  (Delete Accounts)}\! – Please read Doc Descrip. This is a minute not part of an account.  Tailors; books are records of their assemblies, not account books;  refs to money are usually to collections of cash made at these assemblies, and not records of accounting procedures. This record simply minutes an assembly decision that the money brought in for the enrolment of apprentices should be used for paying off the cost of the morris coats.

At this assemblie gregorye Clarke dyd p{ro}misse coven{a}nt and graunte to and w{i}th the wardens [ste] chamberlaynes stewerd{es} and the rest of the bodie of the companie for and duringe the hole terme of fyve yeares ffrom the feast of Saynte Iohn the baptyst next foloinge @f\ foloinge: in {corrected from} t @f\[what does this note mean?] the daye of this asse{m}blie [and] fully to be   complete and endyd to fynde and set goinge in the accustomed pageant of mydsom{er} [..] feaste the gyant, the thre blacke boyes, the bearer of the gyant, and one p{er}son to playe the divells p{ar}te at the prop{er} costes and chargis of the sayed gregorie, as well in victualles of the p{ar}ties aforesayed, as the repayringe of the gyant, and the wagis of all and singular the parties aforesayed and the sayed@f\ and the sayed: {written at bottom left as if a catchword but necessary for sense} @f \ | wardens chamberlaines stewerds and the rest of the bodeye of companie for theire part dothe p{ro}misse coven{a}nt and graunte to and w{i}th the sayed gregorie Clarke that he the sayed gregorie in co{n}sideracion of the aforesayed chargis and travell of the sayed gregorie, shall have the hole vse of the howse and garden whereas nowe the sayed gyant standethe to his proper gayne and co{m}moditie w{i}th licence to lett and sett the same duringe all the terme aforesayed. and besides shall recyve yearlie duringe the terme aforesayed of the sayed wardens Chamberlaynes stewerd{es} and the rest of the companie ten shilling{es} of good and lawfull money of england to be payed at mydsom{er} feast yearelie. and it is agreed that for the repayringe and newe soinge of the gyant{es} coate provision shalbe made that the sayed companie or some of them shall bestowe their labor and payne{s} w{i}thout anie the chargis of the sayed gregorie. And he the sayed gregorie p{ro}massethe coven{a}ntethe and grauntethe the sayed gyant hole and p{er}fect in all his proporcions w{i}th all and singuler his impleme{n}t{es} and appurten{a}nces at the ende of his sayed terme to the sayed wardens chamberlaines stewerdes & the rest of the companie to render and yelde vppe vnder the name of app{ur}tenances as co{n}tayned the divells apparell, and thre payer of slops for the thre blacke boyes.!

At this assemblie it is agreed that the accustomed ffeaste of mydsomer be kepte the next sondaye foloinge the feaste daye of the Natyvitie of Sayncte Iohn Baptist next com{m}inge. @f\next… com{m}inge: {28 June 1573}@f \ and that everye man keepe the olde order appoynted.! 
@l\shall nevar aftar be sete a worke@l \! 
It is also agreed that, for that the iorney men stewerd{es} be slacke in theire dewtie, and to doe and serve at the accustomed ffeaste aforesayed in sutche sort as to the sayed office of the Stewerd{es} of the iornymen belongethe and appertaynethe, any one iornyman or other whatsoever being hereafter by order chosen and admitted to the sayd office, and not servinge the same as he ought to doe, shall never afterward be set a worke by any of the masters or bretheren of this occupacion. and that everye master or brother of this sayed occupacion setting any suche iorneye man so as is aforsayed neglecting his dewtie and deceyvinge the companie. a worke, doe forfett for the same, for everie defalte. twenty shilleng{es} to the vse and behoof of the co{m}panie ...!

@w\f 107v* {(12 June)}\!

The daye and yeare above written The wardens w{i}th certayne of the masters and bretherne to the nu{m}ber of twentye or thereabout{es} met at the Taylers hall, for the choyse of the iorneymen Stewerd{es}. at whiche tyme the iorney men p{re}sentyng them selves there also cho{y}se for their steward{es} Antonye Thacham and henry vp Iame. to whome in consideracion of so short warninge mydsom{er} being so neere at hand the sayed wardens w{i}th the co{n}sent of theire bretherne whose names are here under written allowed and gave owt of the chamber xiij s. iiij d. toward{es} their chargis.!

At this Assemblie Roger Luxmore@f\ Roger Luxmore: {elected steward 9 January 1577/8}@f \ chosen Stewerde by order of this co{m}panie being challenged by the wardens for his slacknes in not fetchinge his moneie appoynted and vsed in this behalffe. and puttinge in sewerties for the same awnswered that he needed not to put in sewerties for the monei whiche he meanethe not to meddell with. and that he colde not tell where to have anie provided for him. he answered that he thanked them yff it twre to a better bargaine. but this bargayne he lyked not. In conclusion he sayed that he wold not kepe or take charge of the ordynarie feast at mydsom{m}er except the co{m}panie wold laye forthe and disburse the moneye for the charge of the same. w{hi}ch yff the co{m}panie wold doe he offered and was content to beare xx s. toward it of his owne chargis. ffor the whiche desobience he was by com{m}on assent of the companie or ^@a\the@a \ greater part of the same. m{er}ced and set to his fyne of payinge of -- v li. to the chamber of this co{m}panie.!

And yt is lykewise agreed that the gyaunt shall be Lett downe and goe nomore. by cause of the charge w{hi}che he causethe yearely to this co{m}panie. And yt is lykewise agreed. that the Stewerds shall fynde the morrys dauncers@f\ dauncers: r {corrected from} s @f \ and their co{m}panie theire sufficient meate and drynke. the mitigation therof to be at the wardens discretion yff theie see cause. the wagis of the sayed Morris dauncers and others to be at the only charge of the chamber of this co{m}panie.!

@w\f 22 {(30 June)}\! 
! 
Where as yt was a greed at the last asemly holden at the tayleers hall the xxix@s\th@s \ of maye that yes geyant from hence forthe shalbe caryd a brode nomore! 
It is a greed now at this assemlye howlden the xxx@s\th@s \ of Iune that whereas gregory clarke at this assembly dothe take vppon him for xv s. by the yeare to be payde vnto him dothe promes to mayntaine the geiant going dvring his life vpon his proper costes and charges and therfore it was a greed by the assemleys consent that the geiant shall goo a gayne and he dothe p{ro}mes farder that at thend of his life the geiant shalbe delivered vnto the cvmpanye a gayne very well repayrd and allso he mvst finde iij blake boys to waite onn the geiant for the same mone a fore seide!

It is agreed at this assembly that the ordinary sole{m}pnite of mid so{m}mer feast. shal be kept. vppon Sondaye being the xxvj of Iune next. And it is agreed that the Stewerds shalbe at the charge of the diet and wagis of the Morris daunsers. It is also agreed. that every brother shall be diligent to acco{m}panie the wardens to the churche. and fro{m} the churche. and everye brother to goe and sytte in his place according to his calling and seniorite. provydid that theye w{hi}ch have borne any office. shall goe according to the place of his office bearinge. althoughe yt be before his senior w{hi}ch hathe borne no office. and the lyke order to be kept in co{m}minge ffrom S@s\te@s \ Iones house to wit ffro{m} Castell gate downward. and every brother of this co{m}panie to enter in to the danc<.> after supp{er} vppon the ffeast daye. and the next daye after. and not to departe before the wardens doe breake of the sayed daunce. the same order for the daunce to be extended to every sister. viz. everye ffremans wife of this co{m}panie. except he have or can allege a reasonable excuse for his or her vppon payne that anie offendinge in any of the p{re}misses. shall forfayte -- xij d. yff he have borne any office. every other p{er}son to forfayte only vj d.!

Presto Cornuto w{hi}ch he never hearde to be taken or construed of anye otherwise then that theye mente thereby to encourage them begg & deliu{er} their trick{es} or feat{es} nimblie quickly & featlye to their praise <...> for his owne parte he never otherwise then in that same conceaved of the said word{es} presto cornuto.!

At this assemblye it is agreed. by co{m}mon assent of the hole assemblye. that the Stewerds of this co{m}pany nowe beinge. and their Successors stewards of this companie for ever hereafter. shall vppon good and speciall co{n}sideracions them moving in this behalfe. have delivered and geven vnto them in ready money owt of the chamber of this co{m}pany. yearely iij li. of laufull money of Englond. that is to say therty shillengs a peece. toward{es} the charge of the accustomed mydso{m}mer feaste of this co{m}panie. w{i}thout any repayment. or yelding of any accompte therfor. in liue and steede. of the stocke before vsed to be delivered vnto them. and repayed. and the sayed Stewards in co{n}sideracions herof shall yearly geve theire severall bands obligatorie to this co{m}panie in severall so{m}mes of vj li. s. d. to kepe and mayntayne the sayed vsuall midso{m}mer feast. at theire owne prop{er} Cost{es} and chargis. and to ffre the co{m}panie of all ma{n}ner of chargis. touching the diet of the sayed feast. And it is farder ordered. enactyd. co{n}descended and decreed by co{m}mon assent. that yff any steward hereafter of this co{m}panie. to be chosen. and receyving the sayed so{m}me of xxx s. for his part in the begynning of the yeare as the meaning is, in co{n}sideracion of the sayed feast. doe happen lewdly to mispend the sayed moneye. or otherwise subtylly and Cautelously to steppe aside or absent. him selffe. and not to p{er}forme the sayed feaste at the tyme appoynted -- [that then] by him selffe. or his assigne. or assignes at his and theire only prop{er} Chargis. that then and in that case. every brother of this co{m}pany [.] in this behalffe offending. shall for that his offens. presently be holden. taken and reputyd. for and as disfranchised of this companie for ever ipso facto. w{i}thout anie more adoe Besides the forfeiture of his band.!

@l\An order for Gillett to bring in the cheynes: etc@l \! 
Whereas Stephen Gillett the musicion dothe demaunde from m{aste}r mayor a ffee for his service att chr{ist}mas w{hi}che hath not byn vsuallie geven heretofore, and hathe receyved from mr mayor Sixe shilling{es} at chr{ist}mas laste, yt is nowe ordered at this assemblye that the sayd Stephen Gillett shall bringe in to mr mayor at the next Auditt the Cheynes of this Cittie and there to Answere the obiecc{i}on, and it is lefte to the discrec{i}on of the mayor and the Auditors to contynue hym in that place or to dismisse hym!

@l\The dayes for the ffeast{es}@l \! 
At this assemblye yt is agreed by the whole assent & consent of this company here p{rese}nte That the gen{er}all ffeaste of this company shalbe holden & kepte vppon the xxiijth daye of Iune & the xxiiijth of Iune next And yt is further agreed by the whole company p{rese}nte That the Chamb{er}leyne of this Corporac{i}on shall delyver vnto  the nowe Steward{es} of this Corporac{i}on viz. Thom{a}s Whythorne & will{ia}m Danyell -- iij li. w{hi}ch shalbe geven them freelye toward{es} theire charges in keepinge the usuall ffeast{es} of this Companye for this yeare The same Steward{es} dischardginge & doing all such chardg{es} as other former steward{es} have done So as the said Steward{es} do firste become bounden vnto this Corporac{i}on for the Doinge & dischardginge the sam{e} two ffeast{es} as other Stewardes have done!

@l\An order that noe playes be on Sabbothe dayes nor after vj of the clock at night@l \! 
At this assemblye yt is ordered that noe Players shalbe from hensfourthe licensed to playe on any Sabbaothe daye nor at any other tyme after sixe of the clocke at nighte, And yf m{aste}r mayor for the tyme beinge shall hereafter p{er}mitte any suche players That then considerat{i}on shalbe hadd for allowance of his penc{i}on And the same to be taken awaye, yf by the opin{i}on & voyc{es} of this howse yt shalbe soe agreed/!

After o{u}r hartie Co{m}mendac{i}ons w{i}th like hope of yo{u}r good helthe &c S{i}r the greate desire that we haue to heare of some good successe in oure longe suyte doth move vs to remember you therin, And so muche the rather for that on monday night last @f\monday night last: {14 May 1610}@f\ there came to o{u}r Citie the prince of Bronnswike sonne to the Duke of Bronnswike and sisters sonne of the Quenes ma{ies}tie, about thr<..> howers before his Co{m}mynge we had notice thereof by a gent{leman} one of [the] ^@a\our@a \ prin<...> folowers who gave intymac{i}on vnto vs that yt was the kinges ma{ies}ties pleasure that we should geve him the best entertaineme{n}t we could for w{hi}ch his ma{jes}tie [wol] would be thankfull vnto us, Whervpon we assembled our selves on the sodaine w{i}th suche nomber of o{u}r Companye as for that p{re}sent we might gett together at his Co{m}mynge we were in redynes at the Counsell house, all the Bell{es} of the Cities & Close did ringe at his Co{m}mynge And by a gyde he was brought through the markett place w{i}th all his folowers w{hi}ch were about .80. horses, when he came against the Counsell house we stode reddy for him; And he p{re}sently came out of Coache and saluted m{aste}r maior And then takinge m{aste}r maior by the hand walked from thence vnto his lodginge to the Antelopp on fote him selff and his folowers, and we did all attend on him to his lodging And when we came thither, we were geven to vnderstand by his [interplete] interpreter that it was his plesure and desire that we sholde all dyne w{i}th him the next daie, and that the next morninge we shold come vnto him and accompany him to the Cathedrall Church to see the same. But the next morninge we had notice that he would ride to willton and see the house there and returne againe to see the Churche before dynner, whervpon we did afterward{es} attend his Co{m}mynge in at Crane bridge, wher at his retorne we beinge ther, he did ther [af] also alight from his horse and all his folowers and walked on foote w{i}th m{aste}r maior vnto the Cathe{dra}ll Churche and the company attended him such as were w{i}th him the night before And when he hadd viewed all the Church Cloyster and Chapter house he walked to the Antelopp to his dynner wher also we kept him company and were kindly entertayned by him by reason thereof we moved his grace (for so he was termed) to be pleased to see our Counsell house p{re}sentlie after dynn{er} and he did willinglie <...>ither wher we had p{re}pared him the best banquett th<..> <...>uld make him for that tyme w{hi}ch he and his Cheiff followers <...> verie good p{ar}te & thankfully Then out of our advised determynac{i}o<.> <...> gave vnto him a fyne purse and tenn pound{es} in good gold in f<..>ther token of our good will; [and] w{hi}ch he also | gratefully receyved lettinge vs to know, that he did hope to see vs more oftener Then we did <...> into his grace by his interpreter that we had made a suyt<.> <...> kinges [for] ma{ies}tie therby to obteyne from him some pryvileg<..> <...> wanted for the better strengthninge of o{u}r owne powers <...> the Citie w{i}thout the w{hi}ch the Citie beinge in a v<.>rye <…>ll hereafter be vtterlye decryed\ and <…> in all Civell governme{n}t and that we desired no more then other Cities like nature hath formerly obteyned. vpon the vnderstandinge thereof we concluded w{i}th this petic{i}on that he wold be so gracious vnto vs ^@a\now@a \ to be our mediator vnto his [med] ma{ies}tie in that behalfe And then he did promys that he would be myndfull of o{u}r request and do vs what good he could w{i}th thys that we had obliged him thervnto by acceptance of our gifte./ And that he would move his ma{ies}tie for vs effect<…> And then his interpreter beinge a gent{leman} of [his] @a\o{u}r king{es} ma{ies}ties@a \ Chamber named Amst<..> Darye did likewise make his faithfull promys vnto vs that he would assuredly call vpon the prince and put him in mynd of o{u}r request [we] as sone as any fitt oportunytie might afford the same/ And thervpon we gave him xx s. in gold to binde him the better to reme{m}ber his p{ro}mys. All w{hi}ch beinge don the princes horses were reddy vnder the Counsell house and then he dep{ar}ted and [rode to] toke his leave and rode to Claringdon p{ar}ke wher he Coursed [d] w{i}th greyhound{es} & kilde a brace of buckes and from there rode to winchester to bedd. And on the next morninge [the] mr will{ia}m Sydenham came vnto vs and told [vp] vs that the prince had bestowed one of those buck{es} vpon m{ast}r maior & his brethren/ [but told vs also that yt was but leane]: Nowe we pray you vpon the receipt hereof to consider on o{u}r behalf what is fitt to be don. And if you so please to advyse w{i}th mr Godfrey @f\mr Godfrey: Richard Godfrey, mayor of Salisbury 1593-4@f\ (if the prince be come to london) that he maye repayre vnto this gent{leman} mr Am<..> Darie And to put him in mynd of o{u}r said request made as aboue at Salisburie and to heare and vnderstand by him what doth insue therof. And further to deale therin as you shall thynke good And for that we feare both yo{u}r self and mr godfrey will come awaye before whitsontide @f\whitsontide: {27—9 May 1610} @f \ w{hi}ch if you both purpose so to do then you will advertize vs therof and signifie yo{u}r pleasure whether any other of o{u}r compan<..> shall come vpp and when to p{re}sente our busihenes either that way or by any other course w{hi}ch you shall thinke good for vs. And <...> desirous of yo{u}r spedyest answere herein we hartely take o{u}r leave and co{m}mytt you to thalmightie, w{i}th o{u}r hartie Co{m}mendac{i}ons to o{u}r lovinge brother & frend mr Richard Godfrey ffro{m} Sa{rum} the 18 of maij 1610 @f\1610: {underlined in} @q\MS@q \@f \!

@l\The ffeast{es}:@l \! 
At this assemblye yt is agreed that the vsuall & accustomed ffeast{es} called the midsomer ffeaste shalbe holden & kepte at the vsuall place vpon the xxiijth & xxiiijth dayes of Iune next ensuinge in suche & lyke mann{er} as the sayd ffeast{es} have byn heretofore kepte by the steward{es} of the Corporac{i}on form{er}lye kepte And in Considerac{i}on thereof the Corporac{i}on are contented to delyver vnto the sayd Steward{es} -- iij li. So as the sayd Steward{es} geve & delyu{er} theire bonde for the p{er}formance thereof!

@h\SAR!1610—11!SPR4\!This record has been moved from below, with revised civic year.
                                                       NB: There are errors in the editing of this record:
1. This material is not from any of the Tailor’s books and should not therefore have a dating period inserted from that source.  It is an independent record from another source – see Doc description, ‘Instructions to the Tailors’, under Guilds and Companies, Tailors.
 2. The folio number should be 89 – see Doc description. To label this ms as ff 1-2 is misleading and unhelpful.  The ms itself is two folios in length.  The book in which it is bound (or mounted) contains a number of mss of different length, but the book’s foliation is sequential throughout, and so to give the foliation as 1-2 would take you to completely the wrong place,  since it is found at f 89 of this book..  
3.  The civic year should be 1610-11.
4.  The date within the bracket should be: 23-28 June 1611.

@l\Iune 23@s\o@s \@l \! 
@l\@i\5.6.& 6.r.3@i@l \! 
@l\@i\1.Iur.sup. 25. Repeale Dc 1. mar. repealed.@i\@l \! 
Vpon Sonday the xxiij@s\th@s \ day of Iune m{aste}r Maior sent his lett{e}r to the wardens and Elders of the corporac{i]on of the Taylors after dynner [to] in these wordes. @P fforasmuch as heretofore the Lordes Sabbaoth day hath bene p{ro}phaned by some ydell and evill disposed p{er}sones w{i}th the Morrys dauncers and drom{m}ers from the churches and in tyme of prayers, yt is thought fitt the same shold [ende] ende and be forborne These are therefore nowe to entreate [y] and also to require youe that youe forbeare further to prophane the sabbath day as heretofore youe have donne eyther w{i}th drom{m}es or Morris dauncers other then in yo{u}r owne private howse, as youe and the Actors therein offendinge shall answere the contrarye Sar{um} the xxiij@s\th@s \ of Iune 1611@f\1611: {underlined in} @q\MS@q \@f \! 
<t4>{(signed)}Barth{olomew} Tokye maior:! 
<t1>To the wardens and elders of the 
Corporac{i}on of Taylors w{i}thin 
the Cittye of newe Sar{um}! 
! 
[Nota est and]! 
Vpon the receipt of this lett{e}r the Wardens sent back to ye Maior fower of the companye to tell him that so <..> soddenlye they cold not stay the goinge forth of the dauncers for that the elders and the company were disp{er}sed and dep{ar}ted, affirming that if they had had but a dayes warninge of his pleasure herein @a\before@a \, they wold [<...>] have conferred thereof w{i}th their company and stayed yt well enoughe, And althoughe they had so short warninge: yet they willed their messengers to tell him that the[y] Morrys dauncers shold not showe them selves that Day before that eveninge prayer shold be donne & ended in all churches And so accordinglye it was p{er}formed, for after the eveninge prayer donne at o{u}r lady churche the whole company came fro{m} thence w{i}th the drom{m}e & Morrys dauncers before them as their ancyent custome was to their hall to supp{er} and [pla] daunced not any more nor any other where els that day. And duringe the tyme of this daunce there was one Izaack Girdler a s{er}vant of m{aste}r Maiors, who whether he came for his pleasure or els to move some quarrell betwene him and some of the companye as lykelye it [was] ^@a\might have bene@a \ amongst suche a company of youth and vnruly Apprentises, we knowe not, but [being] notw{i}thstandinge that he was often & sondry tymes desired to go out fro{m} amongst the company, yet still he crossed the companye contynuallye vntill they came home to their howse p{ro}vokinge the companye as much as he cold to tumult, but by the care & providence of the wardens, there was no tumult nor disorder att all donne.! 
@l\25@l \ 
Vpon Tuesday followinge ye 25@s\th@s \ day. m{aste}r Maior sent Buck one of the bedells [<..>] appoynted to whipp the beggars to the wardens howses to com{m}aund them to come before him, but both of them beinge then Att ye [Guhldl] Guildhall vpon Iuryes heard not of yt & so came not.|! 
@l\Iune 26.@l \! 
Vpon wedensday the 26@s\th@s \ of Iune m{aste}r Maior sent one of the Sergeant{es} (Edw{ard} Knight) for the wardens ^ @a\to ye counsell howse@a \ who came to him accordinglye about ten of the clock before noone. Then he charged them that they had moste ydelye and p{ro}phanelye abused them selves in p{ro}phaninge the Sabbaoth [and] w{i}th many earnest and vrgent speeches and willed them to provyde suretyes [for] to answere it att the next Sessions or els he wold com{m}ytt them to prison. To w{hi}ch they replyed that if they had offended therein they weare@f\ weare: {corrected from} was @f \ sorye for yt, but (as they tooke yt) that if they had p{ro}phaned the Sabbaoth [the ponishement thereof]. @a\it@a \ did not belonge vnto him to inflict any ponyshment vpo{n} them for it. To w{hi}ch he sayd it did. And because they had not obeyed his com{m}aundem{en}t they had made a contempt against him And therefore they shold be com{m}ytted except they wold putt in suretyes to answer yt at the Sessions. They answered that they weare his poore neighboures and desired him not to deale so w{i}th them, for they supposed that that w{hi}ch they did was not mislyked but lyked of by the best in the cittye and what they had donne was donne [for] tyme out of mynde of man and alwayes approved by the best of the cittye. To w{hi}ch m{aste}r Maior sayed And who are the best, can you Iudge who are best@; I am sure no man [but] will allowe of yt if they consider throughlye of [hit] it for it is abomynable before god And hell gapes for such ydle & p{ro}phane fellowes as delyght in it. They told him agayne that ^@a\as@a \ they took yt they thought it no such matt{e}r for w{hi}ch they shold be com{m}ytted to prison well sayd he I will have it so and if [it] [he had] @a\I have@a \ donne otherwise then I @f\ I: {corrected from} he@f \ shold @a\do@a \ [have donne], I@f\ I: {corrected from} he@f \ wyll@f\ wyll: {corrected from} } wold @f \ abyde the shame of yt When they stood com{m}itted and was@f\ and was: {for} and m{aste}r Maior was@f \ goinge away, the wardens desired so much favo{u}r as to go home to their company for an hower or two to conferr w{i}th them upo{n} these matters, promisinge then to come agayne and yeeld them selves, but by no meanes he wold afford them that favo{u}r althoughe they followed him w{i}th their keeper from the Counsell howse to mr Ellyott{e}s corner@f\ mr Ellyotts corner: [[NB IDENTIFY (AR) (possibly in Corporation Ledgers suggests AD in SCL series ; not sure this will be identifiable. AD.]]@f \: And so they went to prison that very day and remayned there vntill Thursday at one of the clock after dynn{e}r at w{hi}ch tyme there came in a wrytten warrant vnder the name of the Maior, mr hutchynes & mr Eyres in these wordes.! 
fforasmuch as Richard Wolford and Edmund watson for some mysdemeanors by them com{m}ytted have bene required to fynde securitye for their good behaviours and also to appeare att the next gen{er}all quarter Sessions to be holden in and for the Cittye of newe Saru{m} aforesayd then and there to answere the p{re}misses w{hi}ch they have and do refuse to do Thes are therfore in his ma{ies}t{ies} name to will & require youe to take into yo{u}r custodye the said Richard wolford & Edmund watson and them safelye to keepe in prison vntill they shall fynde sufficient securitye to his ma{ies}ties vse for their good behaviour and also to appeare att the said Sessions aforesayd And hereof fayle youe not as you [sh] will answere the contrarye Dated at Saru{m} the xxvj@s\th@s \ of Iune 1611! 
<t1>To Roger Luxmore keeper of the prison or gaole 
w{i}thin the Cittye of newe saru{m} aforesayd./|! 
! 
This Mittimus thoughe it beares date ye very day of their com{m}yttment, yet was it not made nor brought to the Gaylor vntill the day following at one of the clock (as aforesayd). And the wardens contynued there in prison vntill ffryday att night ye 28@s\th@s \ day of Iune aforesayd Att w{hi}ch tyme they became bound w{i}th suertyes eyther of them in xx li. a peece & eyther of them suertyes x li. a peece for their apparance at the next quarter Sessions and in the meane tyme to be of good behavyour and so was delyvered!

@w\f 75v  (June 1612 )\! 
...! 
At this assemble it is agreed that the vsyall and accustomed mydsomer feaste shalbe holden & kepte at the vsyall place vppon the syxthe daye of Iulye next beinge mvndaye in suche lycke man{er} as the saied feast haue byn here to fore kepte by the stewerdes of the corporacyon formerly kepte and in consideracyon thereof the corporacyon are contented to delyuer vnto the saied stewardes iij li. soe as the saied stewardes doe gyue and delyu{er} their bond for the p{er}formance thereof!

@w\f 247v {(21 July) (Ordinances)}\! Here is an example of what I find confusing re REED @w\ headings: an editorial head (Ordinances -- above) followed by an actual original head (An order for restraints of plays – below).  Why isn’t the latter the actual heading here, as it usually would be (though editorialized) if this were a c’w account?
...! 
@l\An order for restraynte of playes by night /@l! 
Whereas an order was made in October Anno regni d{omi}ni n{ost}ri Iacobi prime Regis Anglie &c sexto, That noe Players shoulde from thencefourthe be p{er}mitted or licensed to playe on any Sabbaothe daye nor at anye tyme after sixe of the clocke in the night w{i}thin this Cittye, And yf m{aste}r maior for the tyme beinge should p{er}mytt any suche players to playe, That then Considerac{i}on shoulde be hadd [of] for thallowau{n}ce of m{aste}r maiors penc{i}on as by the same order nowe at lardge app{er}ethe yt is nowe at this Councell ordered that the said order shall stande & be in force and shall from hence fourthe p{er}formed vnder the penaltye therein menc{i}oned! 
...!

Ad 14@s\m@s \ Libelli pred{icti} dicit et depo{ni}t That about the latter end of Corne harvest last past and vpon a satterday night then happening, being as she taketh it [the next following] after the playe art{icu}lated and in the dwelling house of Richard Ritche a Turner w{i}thin the parishe of S{ain}t Thomas in the Citty of newe Sarum art{iculate} <...> supra and att a supper there, the tyme and place more Certeyne otherwise she nowe remembereth not as she sayeth, when & where there [w] did some speeches arise happen and growe Conc{er}ning the playe that was Acted [the] @s\vpon@s \ a sonedaye ^ @s\happening@s \ before ^@s\before that tyme@s \ of the baker and the ioyners wife art{iculate}: but what those speeches were she knoweth not neither dothe she nowe remember as she sayeth, for that she then gave litle heede to what was then had or done as she sayeth But nevertheless she sayeth that the art{iculate} Alice Mustian the p{ar}ty def{endan}t in this Cause takinge a piece of pie in her hand [speak] Calling & speaking to one William Ritche a boye of [..] the sayd Richard Ritch{es} and Called him Constable Cosine Constable youe sholld be whipt for the same before youe have done or wordes to the same effect And she ffarder sayeth and deposeth that the s{ay}d Alice Mustian speaking of and meaning the art{iculate} Robert Humphries, and Mary Robert{es} the party plaintiffe as she verily beleeveth and is verily p{er}swaded in her Conscience the sayd Alice Mustian then sayd That if they had been punished or Carted as mr Hutchins (one of his Ma{jes}ties Iustices of peace) woulde have <...> then this thing or this playe never need to have been & to the same effect the wordes more Certeyneley she nowe remembreth not being uttered & spoken as she beleeveth to the hurte distress shame and reproache of the s{ay}d Mary Robertes In the presens sight and hearing of this depo{nen}t, Richard Ritche his wife & W{illia}m Ritche afores{ay}d...!

@m\To the right w{orshipfu}ll the Maior, Recorder, and others the Iustices of peace and Magistrat{es} of the Cittie of New Saru{m}@m \! 
@m\The humble Petition of William Madge@m \! 
Shewing yt at the last gen{er}all Councell Io{hn} Bacon, Edw{ard} Madge, William Richardson, & W{illia}m Davyes being by yo{u}r wor{shi}ps appoyntm{en}t to play in each others Company, and their names entred in a booke accordinglie.! 
W{illia}m Davyes is but a Learner of his art, never served any tyme of Apprenticeshipp, nor in the Company before then, and is not sufficient for the place, w{hi}ch yo{u}r petic{i}on{er} will make appeare if yo{u}r wor{shi}ps please to have him tryed before sufficient Musitians! 
Moreover at a Conuocac{i}on on the ffourth of November last, it pleased some of yo{u}r wor{shi}ps to resolve, that if the said davies were insufficient hee should bee dismissed the Company at the next gen{er}all Councell, & another more sufficient to bee in his place.! 
It is for that yo{u}r petic{i}on{er} hath been his brothers Apprentice & se{r}ved in the Company theis 8 yeeres past and is now free, but his name not entred in the booke, nor leave graunted him to weare one of the Chaynes! 
[[INDE NT BLOCK]] Therefore humblie prayeth yo{u}r wor{shi}ps favor soe to give order that yo{u}r Petic{i}on{er}s name may bee entred in the booke next after W{illia}m Richardson, and may by the same order have his place allowed him, & obteyne [<.>] leave of yo{u}r wor{shi}ps to weare a Chayne w{i}th the rest of the Company!  
@i\will{ia}m medge to wear the Chayne ^@a\soe long as he shall behaue hymsel well@a \ but davyes share to continewe as before: & to haue a Coate/ & medg{es} boy to [Wante] <...> be p{ro}vided by hymself the rest to haue coates their being 6 <..>lowed by the Cha{m}ber/@i\!

NB: Below is the record of a transcription made by Isaac Walton from the original Close record itself (see Doc Descrip); it was apparently omitted from the Adobe text records. A copy of Walton’s transcription was given to me by Suzanne Ewart, former Cathedral archivist.  Under the restrictive rules then in place I was not privileged to see the original transcription, or to obtain a photocopy, and hence I have no idea of its placing on the page. It was checked in situ by REED though, for accuracy of content.  Should it just be left as is (i.e., unedited by REED,  since it isn’t an original ms) and noted as an antiquarian entry? AD

...one Desired me to walk to the Church-yard, where I should see good sport with the Searching woman and the Bearers; I came to a place where I could see and hear them, and when I came I found the four Bearers, each of them having on their shoulders, a Thurndel-pot of ale, and the woman had on her head a Thurndel-pot of Ale. These five were dancing amongst the Graves, singing, Hie for more Shoulder-work,@f \ Hie … Shoulder-work: {underlined in} @q\MS@q \! @f \ in a fearful manner, and when they saw me, they ran away. Shortly after one of them died, which put me to much care for another, for then the Plague@f\ Plague: {underlined in} @q\MS@q \ @f \ did much increase, and in that summer died nine Bearers.!

@h\SAR!{c}1633--4!SMP2\! 
@w\single sheet* {(Concerning the parsonage)}\! 
! 
The Rectory, or Parsonage of St Thomas P{a}rish (whereof the Deane and Chapter of Sarum are Patrons, and Proprietors) consists of! 
1. Tithes of [lands and] gardens within the p{a}rish! 
2. The Easter Booke! 
3. Offering at Weddings, Church-goeings, and Burialls! 
The Church-wardens and p{a}rishioners (as lessees or Procurators to the Deane and Chapter) haue euer since 5. & 6.@f \ 5. & 6.: {ie, 5 and 6 Philip and Mary, 25 July--17 November 1558}@f \ receiued all the p{ro}fits of the p{ar}sonage, towards the Reparation, and other charges of the church, at a yearly rent, [the rent hath bene] and haue likewise payed the Curates, Clarke, and Sextons wages; [ou]! 
From 5. & 6. @f\5. & 6.: {ie, 5 and 6 Philip and Mary, 25 July--17 November 1558}@f \ till this day, the Churchwardens [ha] Accounts haue bene generall all in one, as well for other p{ro}fits of the Church, as for the dues of the Parsonage, [and] but vnder seuerall Titles;! 
There are seuerall duties w{hi}ch the Churchwardens haue euer receiued to the vse, and for the maintenance of the Church, w{hi}ch doe not belonge vnto the Parsonage, namely, Gatherings at Hocktide, and Whitsontide, Offerings on Good Fryday, and mony for Graues, Seates, and Ringinge of Bells at Funeralls;! 
And that these things belonge not to the P{ar}sonage, it appeares by the seuerall Accounts of the Churchwardens at such times as the Parish medled not with the Parsonage;! 
For in 38@s\o@s \ H 8.@f\ 38@s\o@s\ H 8.: {ie, 38 Henry VIII, 22 April 1546--28 January 1547}! @f \ they account for [all] those duties only, and not for any tithes, Easter booke, or Offerings; nor did they then pay any rent to the Deane and Chapter, or pay the Curate, or Clarke any wages;! 
Thus is continued till 5. & 6.@f\ 5. & 6.: {ie, 5 and 6 Philip and Mary, 25 July--17 November 1558}@f \ And then the churchwardens Account for the P{ro}fits of the P{ar}sonage, as well as the other dutyes; and demaund allowance for the rent[,] payed to the Deane and Chapter, and for the Curats, and Clarks wages; And in this maner it hath continued euer since! 
...!

@h\SAR!1638--9!SBL5\! 
@w\f 15v {(May)}\! 
...! 
At Salisbury 1639 a iolly fellow brued strong Ale to maintaine Sport on the Lords day and in the month of May would have a Maypole set vp on the Lords day and on the night before he and his ioviall Crew went in despight of the puritans to Cvt the tree and on the Lords day in the morning he driuing his three horses downe the hill a littel beyound Salisbury@f\ driuing … beyond Salisbury: {probably coming down Harnham hill south of Salisbury, headed for Harnham bridge}@f \ to come to Salisbury the tree not being tyed fast in the Cart turned round by reason of one whele going higher than the other, & so fell over beate out the fellowes braines abroad vpon the ground, and there ended their sport and instead of a madmerrymaking of the maygame had the sad burying of a profaine fellow and the Horse and Cart forfeit!
